Page 1
Pakistan 
Coordinates: [URL: "https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Pakistan&params=30_N_70_E_type:country_region:PK"] 30°N 70°E
Pakistan,[c] officially the Islamic Republic of Pakistan,[d] is a
country in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia. It is the world's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population"] fifth-most populous country,
 with a population of almost 242 million, and has the world's second-
 largest Muslim population.[13] Pakistan is the 33rd-largest country by
area, spanning 881,913 square kilometres (340,509 square miles). It
has a 1,046-kilometre (650-mile) coastline along the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Sea"] Arabian Sea and
 Gulf of Oman in the south, and is bordered by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India"] India to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India%E2%80%93Pakistan_border"] the east,
 Afghanistan to the west, Iran to the southwest, and China to the
northeast. It is separated narrowly from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajikistan"] Tajikistan by Afghanistan's
 Wakhan Corridor in the north, and also shares a maritime border with
Oman.
Pakistan is the site of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Pakistan"] several ancient cultures, including the 8,500-
 year-old Neolithic site of Mehrgarh in Balochistan,[14] and the Indus
Valley Civilisation of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronze_Age"] Bronze Age, the most extensive of the
civilisations of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afro-Eurasia"] Afro-Eurasia.[15][16] The region that comprises the
modern state of Pakistan was the realm of multiple empires and
 dynasties, including the Achaemenid; briefly that of Alexander the
Great; the Seleucid, the Maurya, the Kushan, the Gupta;[17] the
 Umayyad Caliphate in its southern regions, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Shahis"] Hindu Shahis, the
Ghaznavids, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate"] Delhi Sultanate, the Mughals,[18] the Durranis, the
 Sikh Empire, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Company_rule_in_India"] British East India Company rule, and most recently, the
 British Indian Empire from 1858 to 1947. 
Islamic Republic of Pakistan

Spurred by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Movement"] Pakistan Movement, which sought a homeland for the
 Muslims of British India, and election victories in 1946 by the All-
India Muslim League, Pakistan gained independence in 1947 after the
 Partition of the British Indian Empire, which awarded separate
statehood to its Muslim-majority regions and was accompanied by an
unparalleled mass migration and loss of life.[19] Initially a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan"] Dominion
 of the British Commonwealth, Pakistan officially drafted its
constitution in 1956, and emerged as a declared [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_republic"] Islamic republic. In
1971, the exclave of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Pakistan"] East Pakistan seceded as the new country of
 Bangladesh after a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War"] nine-month-long civil war. In the following four
decades, Pakistan has been ruled by governments whose descriptions,
although complex, commonly alternated between civilian and military,
democratic and authoritarian, relatively [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secularism_in_Pakistan"] secular and Islamist.[20]
Pakistan elected a civilian government in 2008, and in 2010 adopted a
 parliamentary system with periodic elections.[21]
Pakistan is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power"] regional[22][23][24] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_power"] middle power nation,[25][26][27]
and has the world's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel"] sixth-largest standing armed forces. It is a declared
 nuclear-weapons state, and is ranked amongst the emerging and
growth-leading economies,[28] with a large and rapidly-growing
middle class.[29] Pakistan's political history since independence has
been characterised by periods of significant economic and military
growth as well as those of political and economic instability. It is an
 ethnically and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_Pakistan"] linguistically diverse country, with similarly diverse
 geography and wildlife. The country continues to face challenges,
including poverty, illiteracy, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption_in_Pakistan"] corruption and terrorism.[30] Pakistan is a
 member of the United Nations, the Shanghai Cooperation
Organisation, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation"] Organisation of Islamic Cooperation, the

Etymology
The name [URL: "https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Pakistan"] Pakistan literally means "land of the pure" or "land of purity", in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu"] Urdu and Persian.[31] It alludes to the word
 ‎پاک (pāk), meaning "pure" in Persian and Pashto.[32] The suffix [URL: "https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D9%80%D8%B3%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%86#Persian"] ‎ـستان (transliterated in English as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/-stan"] -stan) is from Persian,
and means "land" or "place of".[33][34][35]
The name of the country was coined in 1933 by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choudhry_Rahmat_Ali"] Choudhry Rahmat Ali, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Movement"] Pakistan Movement activist, who published it in
a pamphlet [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Declaration"] Now or Never, using it as an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acronym"] acronym ("thirty million Muslim brethren who live in PAKISTAN")[36] to refer
to the names of the five northern regions of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Raj"] British Raj: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab_Province_(British_India)"] Punjab, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North-West_Frontier_Province_(1901%E2%80%932010)"] Afghania, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(princely_state)"] Kashmir, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sind_Province_(1936%E2%80%9355)"] Sindh, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baluchistan_(Chief_Commissioner%27s_Province)"] Baluchistan.[36]
History
Early and medieval age
Indus Priest King Statue
from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-Daro"] Mohenjo-Daro. 
Some of the earliest ancient human civilisations in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia originated from areas
encompassing present-day Pakistan.[37] The earliest known inhabitants in the region were
 Soanian during the Lower Paleolithic, of whom stone tools have been found in the Soan
Valley of Punjab.[38] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_River"] Indus region, which covers most of present day Pakistan, was
the site of several successive ancient cultures including the Neolithic Mehrgarh[39] and the
Bronze Age [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation"] Indus Valley Civilisation[40][41] (2,800–1,800 BCE) at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harappa"] Harappa and
 Mohenjo-Daro.[42]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedic_period"] Vedic period (1500–500 BCE) was characterised by an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Aryan_peoples"] Indo-Aryan culture; during
this period the Vedas, the oldest scriptures associated with Hinduism, were composed, and
this culture later became well established in the region.[43] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multan"] Multan was an important Hindu
pilgrimage centre.[44] The Vedic civilisation flourished in the ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gandhara"] Gandhāran city of
Takṣaśilā, now [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxila"] Taxila in the Punjab, which was founded around 1000 BCE.[45][39]
 Successive ancient empires and kingdoms ruled the region: the Persian Achaemenid
 Empire (around 519 BCE), Alexander the Great's empire in 326 BCE[46] and the Maurya
Page 4
 Empire, founded by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandragupta_Maurya"] Chandragupta Maurya and extended by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashoka_the_Great"] Ashoka the Great, until
185 BCE. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Greek_Kingdom"] Indo-Greek Kingdom founded by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demetrius_I_of_Bactria"] Demetrius of Bactria (180–165 BCE)
included Gandhara and Punjab and reached its greatest extent under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menander_I"] Menander (165–
150 BCE), prospering the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Buddhism"] Greco-Buddhist culture in the region.[39][47] Taxila had one of
the earliest universities and centres of higher education in the world, which was
established during the late Vedic period in 6th century BCE.[48][49] The school consisted
of several monasteries without large dormitories or lecture halls where the religious
instruction was provided on an individualistic basis.[49] The ancient university was
documented by the invading forces of Alexander the Great and was also recorded by
Chinese pilgrims in the 4th or 5th century CE.[50]
At its zenith, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rai_Dynasty"] Rai Dynasty (489–632 CE) of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sindh"] Sindh ruled this region and the
surrounding territories.[51] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pala_Dynasty"] Pala Dynasty was the last Buddhist empire, which, under
 Dharmapala and Devapala, stretched across South Asia from what is now [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangladesh"] Bangladesh
through [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_India"] Northern India to Pakistan.
Islamic conquest 
 Standing Buddha from
 Gandhara, Greco-Buddhist
art, 1st–2nd century AD.
The Arab conqueror [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Qasim"] Muhammad ibn Qasim conquered Sindh in 711 CE.[52][53] The
Pakistan government's official chronology claims this as the time when the foundation of Pakistan was laid[52][54] but the
concept of Pakistan arrived in the 19th century. The Early Medieval period (642–1219 CE) witnessed the spread of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam"] Islam
in the region. During this period, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sufi"] Sufi [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dawah"] missionaries played a pivotal role in converting a majority of the regional Buddhist
 and Hindu population to Islam.[55] Upon the defeat of the Turk and Hindu Shahi dynasties which governed the Kabul
 Valley, Gandhara (present-day Khyber Pakhtunkwa), and western Punjab in the 7th to 11th centuries CE, several
successive Muslim empires ruled over the region, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghaznavids"] Ghaznavid Empire (975–1187 CE), the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghorid"] Ghorid Kingdom,
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate"] Delhi Sultanate (1206–1526 CE). The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lodi_dynasty"] Lodi dynasty, the last of the Delhi Sultanate, was replaced by the Mughal
Empire (1526–1857 CE). 
The Mughals introduced Persian literature and high culture, establishing
the roots of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Persian_culture"] Indo-Persian culture in the region.[56] In the region of
modern-day Pakistan, key cities during the Mughal period were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahore"] Lahore
and Thatta,[57] both of which were chosen as the site of impressive
 Mughal buildings.[58] In the early 16th century, the region remained
under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal Empire.[59]
 Badshahi Mosque, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahore"] Lahore 
In the 18th century, the slow disintegration of the Mughal Empire was
 hastened by the emergence of the rival powers of the Maratha
 Confederacy and later the Sikh Empire, as well as invasions by Nader
Shah from Iran in 1739 and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durrani_Empire"] Durrani Empire of Afghanistan in 1759.
The growing political power of the British in Bengal had not yet reached
the territories of modern Pakistan.
Colonial period
None of the territory of modern Pakistan was ruled by the British, or other European powers, until 1839, when Karachi,
then a small fishing village with a mud fort guarding the harbour, was taken, and held as an enclave with a port and
 military base for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Afghan_War"] First Afghan War that soon followed. The rest of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sindh"] Sindh was taken in 1843, and in the following
decades, first the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_East_India_Company"] East India Company, and then after the post-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepoy_Mutiny"] Sepoy Mutiny (1857–1858) direct rule of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queen_Victoria"] Queen Victoria of
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire"] British Empire, took over most of the country partly through wars, and also treaties. The main wars were that against
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baloch_people"] Baloch [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talpur_dynasty"] Talpur dynasty, ended by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Miani"] Battle of Miani (1843) in Sindh, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Sikh_War_(disambiguation)"] Anglo-Sikh Wars (1845–1849) and the
 Anglo-Afghan Wars (1839–1919). By 1893, all modern Pakistan was part of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Indian_Empire"] British Indian Empire, and remained so
until independence in 1947.
 Under the British, modern Pakistan was mostly divided into the Sind Division, Punjab Province, and the Baluchistan
Agency. There were various [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princely_state"] princely states, of which the largest was Bahawalpur.
Page 5
A [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857"] rebellion in 1857 called the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepoy_mutiny"] Sepoy mutiny of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengal"] Bengal was the
region's major armed struggle against the British.[60] Divergence in
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu%E2%80%93Islamic_relations"] relationship between Hinduism and Islam created a major rift in
 British India that led to motivated religious violence in British
India.[61] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindi%E2%80%93Urdu_controversy"] language controversy further escalated the tensions
between Hindus and Muslims.[62] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengali_Renaissance"] Hindu renaissance witnessed
an awakening of intellectualism in traditional [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism"] Hinduism and saw the
emergence of more assertive influence in the social and political
spheres in British India.[63] A [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aligarh_Movement"] Muslim intellectual movement,
founded by Sir [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syed_Ahmed_Khan"] Syed Ahmed Khan to counter the Hindu renaissance,
envisioned as well as advocated for the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two-nation_theory"] two-nation theory[64] and led
to the creation of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-India_Muslim_League"] All-India Muslim League in 1906. In contrast
to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_National_Congress"] Indian National Congress's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-British_sentiment"] anti-British efforts, the Muslim
League was a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglomania"] pro-British movement whose political program
 inherited the British values that would shape Pakistan's future civil
society.[65] The largely non-violent independence struggle led by the
Indian Congress engaged millions of protesters in mass campaigns of
 civil disobedience in the 1920s and 1930s against the British
Empire.[66][67] 
Sir [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syed_Ahmad_Khan"] Syed Ahmad Khan
(1817–1898), whose
 vision formed the basis
of Pakistan 
 Muhammad Ali Jinnah
(1876–1948) served as
Pakistan's first
Governor-General and
the leader of the
 Pakistan Movement
The Muslim League slowly rose to mass popularity in the 1930s amid fears of
under-representation and neglect by the British of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Muslims"] Indian Muslims in politics.
In his presidential address of 29 December 1930, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Iqbal"] Allama Iqbal called for "the
amalgamation of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwestern_India"] North-West Muslim-majority Indian states" consisting of Punjab,
 North-West Frontier Province, Sind, and Baluchistan.[68] The perceived neglect of
Muslim interests by Congress led British [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1937_Indian_provincial_elections"] provincial governments during the period
of 1937–39 convinced [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_Jinnah"] Muhammad Ali Jinnah, the founder of Pakistan to espouse
the two-nation theory and led the Muslim League to adopt the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahore_Resolution"] Lahore Resolution
of 1940 presented by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sher-e-Bangla"] Sher-e-Bangla [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.K._Fazlul_Haque"] A.K. Fazlul Haque, popularly known as the
 Pakistan Resolution.[64] In World War II, Jinnah and British-educated founding
fathers in the Muslim League supported the United Kingdom's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_in_World_War_II"] war efforts,
countering opposition against it whilst working towards Sir Syed's vision.[69] 
 Clock Tower, Faisalabad, built by the
British government in the 19th
century
Pakistan Movement
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1946_Indian_provincial_elections"] 1946 elections resulted in the Muslim League winning 90 percent of the seats reserved for Muslims. Thus, the 1946
election was effectively a plebiscite in which the Indian Muslims were to vote on the creation of Pakistan, a plebiscite won
by the Muslim League. This victory was assisted by the support given to the Muslim League by the support of the
landowners of Sindh and Punjab. The Indian National Congress, which initially denied the Muslim League's claim of
being the sole representative of Indian Muslims, was now forced to recognise the fact.[70] The British had no alternative
except to take Jinnah's views into account as he had emerged as the sole spokesperson of the entirety of British India's
Muslims. However, the British [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_the_partition_of_India"] did not want colonial India to be partitioned, and in one last effort to prevent it, they
devised the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_Mission_Plan"] Cabinet Mission plan.[71]
As the cabinet mission failed, the British government announced its intention to end the British Rule in 1946–47.[72]
 Nationalists in British India—including Jawaharlal Nehru and Abul Kalam Azad of Congress, Jinnah of the All-India
Muslim League, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Master_Tara_Singh"] Master Tara Singh representing the Sikhs—agreed to the proposed terms of transfer of power and
independence in June 1947 with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor-General_of_India"] Viceroy of India, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma"] Lord Mountbatten of Burma.[73] As the United Kingdom agreed to
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_India"] partitioning of India in 1947, the modern state of Pakistan was established on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourteenth_of_August"] 14 August 1947 (27th of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramadan"] Ramadan in 1366
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Calendar"] Islamic Calendar), amalgamating the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_India"] Muslim-majority eastern and northwestern regions of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_India"] British India.[67] It
comprised the provinces of Balochistan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Bengal"] East Bengal, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North-West_Frontier_Province_(1901%E2%80%931955)"] North-West Frontier Province, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan"] West Punjab, and Sindh.[64][73]
In the riots that accompanied the partition in Punjab Province, it is believed that between 200,000 and 2,000,000[74]
people were killed in what some have described as a retributive genocide between the religions[75] while 50,000 Muslim
women were [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violence_against_women_during_the_partition_of_India"] abducted and raped by Hindu and Sikh men, 33,000 Hindu and Sikh women also experienced the same fate
Page 6
at the hands of Muslims.[76] Around 6.5 million Muslims moved from India to West Pakistan and 4.7 million Hindus and
Sikhs moved from West Pakistan to India.[77] It was the largest mass migration in human history.[78] A subsequent dispute
over the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princely_state"] princely state of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(princely_state)"] Jammu and Kashmir eventually sparked the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1947%E2%80%931948"] Indo-Pakistani War of 1947–1948.[79]
Independence and modern Pakistan
After [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creation_of_Pakistan"] independence in 1947, Jinnah, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Party_chair"] President of the Muslim League, became the
nation's first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor-General_of_Pakistan"] Governor-General as well as the first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speaker_of_the_National_Assembly_of_Pakistan"] President-Speaker of the Parliament,
but he died of tuberculosis on 11 September 1948.[80] Meanwhile, Pakistan's founding
fathers agreed to appoint [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liaquat_Ali_Khan"] Liaquat Ali Khan, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secretary_General"] secretary-general of the party, the
nation's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Pakistan"] first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan"] Prime Minister. From 1947 to 1956, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monarchy_of_Pakistan"] Pakistan was a monarchy within the
Commonwealth of Nations, and had two monarchs before it became a republic.[81]
The creation of Pakistan was never fully
accepted by many British leaders, among them
 Lord Mountbatten.[83] Mountbatten clearly
expressed his lack of support and faith in the
Muslim League's idea of Pakistan.[84] Jinnah
 Queen Elizabeth II was the last
monarch of independent
Pakistan, before it became a
republic in 1956. 
refused Mountbatten's  offer to serve as
 Governor-General of Pakistan.[85] When
Mountbatten was asked by Collins and
Lapierre if he would have sabotaged Pakistan
had he known that Jinnah was dying of
tuberculosis, he replied 'most probably'.[86] 
The American [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency"] CIA film on Pakistan
made in 1950 examines the history
and geography of Pakistan.
Maulana [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shabbir_Ahmad_Usmani"] Shabbir Ahmad Usmani, a respected Deobandi alim (scholar) who
occupied the position of Shaykh al-Islam in Pakistan in 1949,
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abul_A%27la_Maududi"] Maulana Mawdudi of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamaat-e-Islami"] Jamaat-i-Islami played a pivotal role
in the demand for an Islamic constitution. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abul_A%27la_Maududi"] Mawdudi demanded
that the Constituent Assembly make an explicit declaration
affirming the "supreme sovereignty of God" and the
supremacy of the shariah in Pakistan.[87] 
"You are free; you are free to go to your temples,
you are free to go to your mosques or to any other
place or worship in this State of Pakistan. You may
belong to any religion or caste or creed – that has
nothing to do with the business of the State."
A significant result of the efforts of the Jamaat-i-Islami and the
 ulama was the passage of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Objectives_Resolution"] Objectives Resolution in March
1949. The Objectives Resolution, which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liaquat_Ali_Khan"] Liaquat Ali Khan
called the second most important step in Pakistan's history, 
—[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_Jinnah"] Muhammad Ali Jinnah's first speech to the
Constituent Assembly of Pakistan[82]
declared that "sovereignty over the entire universe belongs to
God Almighty alone and the authority which He has delegated
to the State of Pakistan through its people for being exercised within the limits prescribed by Him is a sacred trust". The
Objectives Resolution has been incorporated as a preamble to the constitutions of 1956, 1962, and 1973.[88]
 Democracy was stalled by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958_Pakistani_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] martial law that had been enforced by President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iskander_Mirza"] Iskander Mirza, who was replaced by the
 army chief, General [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayub_Khan_(President_of_Pakistan)"] Ayub Khan. After adopting a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Pakistan_of_1962"] presidential system in 1962, the country experienced exceptional
growth until a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1965"] second war with India in 1965 that led to an economic downturn and wide-scale [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tashkent_Agreement"] public disapproval in
1967.[89][90] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legal_Framework_Order,_1970"] Consolidating control from Ayub Khan in 1969, President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yahya_Khan"] Yahya Khan had to deal with a devastating
 cyclone that caused 500,000 deaths in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Pakistan"] East Pakistan.[91]
In 1970 Pakistan held its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_Pakistani_general_election"] first democratic elections since independence, meant to mark a transition from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legal_Framework_Order,_1970"] military rule to
democracy, but after the East Pakistani [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awami_League"] Awami League won against the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Peoples_Party"] Pakistan Peoples Party (PPP), Yahya Khan and
the military establishment refused to hand over power.[92][93] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Searchlight"] Operation Searchlight, a military crackdown on the Bengali
 nationalist movement, led to a declaration of independence and the waging of a war of liberation by the Bengali Mukti
Bahini forces in East Pakistan,[93][94] which in West Pakistan was described as a civil war as opposed to a war of
liberation.[95]
Independent researchers estimate that between 300,000 and 500,000 civilians died during this period while the
Bangladesh government puts the number of dead at three million,[96] a figure that is now nearly universally regarded as
excessively inflated.[97] Some academics such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudolph_Rummel"] Rudolph Rummel and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rounaq_Jahan"] Rounaq Jahan say both sides[98] committed
Page 7
genocide; others such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Richard_Sisson"] Richard Sisson and Leo E. Rose believe there was no
genocide.[99] In response to India's support for the insurgency in East Pakistan,
 preemptive strikes on India by Pakistan's air force, navy, and marines sparked a
conventional war in 1971 that resulted in an Indian victory and East Pakistan gaining
 independence as Bangladesh.[93]
With Pakistan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instrument_of_Surrender_(1971)"] surrendering in the war, Yahya Khan was replaced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto"] Zulfikar Ali Bhutto
as president; the country worked towards promulgating [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Pakistan"] its constitution and putting the
country on the road to democracy. Democratic rule resumed from 1972 to 1977—an era of
self-consciousness, intellectual leftism, nationalism, and nationwide reconstruction.[100] In
1972 Pakistan embarked on an ambitious plan to develop its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_and_its_Nuclear_Deterrent_Program"] nuclear deterrence capability
with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutually_assured_destruction"] the goal of preventing any [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_interventionism"] foreign invasion; the country's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KANUPP"] first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant"] nuclear power plant
 was inaugurated in that same year.[101][102] Accelerated in response to India's first nuclear
test in 1974, this [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_and_Nuclear_Weapons"] crash program was completed in 1979.[102]
 Democracy ended with a military coup in 1977 against the leftist PPP, which saw General
Zia-ul-Haq become the president in 1978. From 1977 to 1988, President Zia's
 corporatisation and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamization_of_Economy"] economic Islamisation initiatives led to Pakistan becoming one of the
 fastest-growing economies in South Asia.[103] While building up the country's nuclear
program, increasing Islamisation,[104] and the rise of a homegrown [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_in_Pakistan"] conservative 
 Signing of the Tashkent
Declaration to end [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1965"] hostilities
with India in 1965 in
Tashkent, USSR, by
President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_Marshal_Ayub_Khan"] Ayub alongside
 Bhutto (centre) and Aziz
philosophy, Pakistan helped subsidise and distribute US [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Cyclone"] resources to factions of the
 mujahideen against the USSR's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War"] intervention in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Afghanistan"] communist Afghanistan.[105] Pakistan's 
Ahmed (left)
 North-West Frontier Province became a base for the anti-Soviet Afghan fighters, with the
province's influential [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deobandi"] Deobandi ulama playing a significant role in encouraging and organising the 'jihad'.[106]
 President Zia died in a plane crash in 1988, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto"] Benazir Bhutto, daughter of Zulfikar Ali Bhutto, was elected as the
country's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Muslim_societies"] first female Prime Minister. The PPP was followed by conservative [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Muslim_League_(N)"] Pakistan Muslim League (N), and over the
next decade the leaders of the two parties fought for power, alternating in office while the country's situation worsened;
economic indicators fell sharply, in contrast to the 1980s. This period is marked by prolonged stagflation, instability,
corruption, nationalism, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geostrategy"] geopolitical rivalry with India, and the clash of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism_in_Pakistan"] left wing-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_in_Pakistan"] right wing ideologies.[107] As [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Muslim_League_(N)"] PML (N)
secured a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermajority"] supermajority in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997_Pakistani_general_election"] elections in 1997, Sharif authorised [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_nuclear_weapons_tests_of_Pakistan"] nuclear testings (See:[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chagai-I"] Chagai-I and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chagai-II"] Chagai-II), as a
 retaliation to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pokhran-II"] second nuclear tests ordered by India, led by Prime Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee"] Atal Bihari Vajpayee in May 1998.[108]
 Military tension between the two countries in the Kargil district led to the Kargil
 War of 1999, and turmoil in civic-military relations allowed General Pervez
Musharraf to take over through a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Pakistani_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] bloodless coup d'état.[109][110] Musharraf
governed Pakistan as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government"] chief executive from 1999 to 2001 and as President from
 2001 to 2008—a period of enlightenment, social liberalism, extensive economic
reforms,[111] and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan%27s_role_in_the_War_on_Terror"] direct involvement in the US-led war on terrorism. When the
 National Assembly historically completed its first full five-year term on 15
November 2007, the new elections were called by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Election_Commission_of_Pakistan"] Election Commission.[112]
President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_W._Bush"] George W. Bush meets
with President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pervez_Musharraf"] Musharraf in
 Islamabad during his 2006 visit to
Pakistan. 
After the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Benazir_Bhutto"] assassination of Benazir Bhutto in 2007, the PPP secured the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majority"] most votes
in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Pakistani_general_election"] elections of 2008, appointing party member [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yousaf_Raza_Gillani"] Yousaf Raza Gillani as Prime
Minister.[113] Threatened with impeachment, President Musharraf resigned on 18
August 2008, and was succeeded by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asif_Ali_Zardari"] Asif Ali Zardari.[114] Clashes with the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan"] judicature prompted Gillani's disqualification from the Parliament and as the Prime
Minister in June 2012.[115] By its own financial calculations, Pakistan's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan%27s_role_in_the_War_on_Terror"] involvement in the war on terrorism has cost up to
$118 billion,[116] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_terrorist_incidents_in_Pakistan_since_2001"] sixty thousand casualties and more than 1.8 million displaced civilians.[117] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_Pakistani_general_election"] general election held in
2013 saw the PML (N) almost achieve a supermajority, following which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nawaz_Sharif"] Nawaz Sharif was elected as the Prime Minister,
returning to the post for the third time in fourteen years, in a democratic transition.[118] In 2018, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imran_Khan"] Imran Khan (the chairman
of PTI) won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Pakistan_general_election"] 2018 Pakistan general election with 116 general seats and became the 22nd [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan"] Prime Minister of Pakistan in
election of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Pakistan"] National Assembly of Pakistan for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister"] Prime Minister by getting 176 votes against [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shehbaz_Sharif"] Shehbaz Sharif (the chairman of
 PML (N)) who got 96 votes.[119] In April 2022, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shehbaz_Sharif"] Shehbaz Sharif was elected as Pakistan's new prime minister, after Imran
Khan lost a no-confidence vote in the parliament.[120]
Role of Islam
Page 8
Pakistan is the only country to have been created in the name of Islam.[121] The idea of Pakistan, which had received
overwhelming popular support among Indian Muslims, especially those in the provinces of British India where Muslims
were in a minority such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Provinces_(1937%E2%80%9350)"] United Provinces,[122] was articulated in terms of an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_state"] Islamic state by the Muslim League
leadership, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulama"] ulama (Islamic clergy) and Jinnah.[123] Jinnah had developed a close association with the ulama and upon
his death was described by one such alim, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maulana_Shabbir_Ahmad_Usmani"] Maulana Shabbir Ahmad Usmani, as the greatest Muslim after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aurangzeb"] Aurangzeb and
as someone who desired to unite the Muslims of the world under the banner of Islam.[124]
The Objectives Resolution in March 1949, which declared God as the sole sovereign over the entire universe, represented
the first formal step to transform Pakistan into an Islamic state.[125][88] Muslim League leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaudhry_Khaliquzzaman"] Chaudhry Khaliquzzaman
asserted that Pakistan could only truly become an Islamic state after bringing all believers of Islam into a single political
unit.[126] Keith Callard, one of the earliest scholars on Pakistani politics, observed that Pakistanis believed in the essential
unity of purpose and outlook in the Muslim world and assumed that Muslim from other countries would share their views
on the relationship between religion and nationality.[127]
However, Pakistan's pan-Islamist sentiments for a united Islamic bloc called
Islamistan were not shared by other Muslim governments,[128] although Islamists
such as the Grand Mufti of Palestine, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amin_al-Husseini"] Al-Haj Amin al-Husseini, and leaders of the
 Muslim Brotherhood, became drawn to the country. Pakistan's desire for an
international organization of Muslim countries was fulfilled in the 1970s when the
 Organization of Islamic Conference (OIC) was formed.[129]
The strongest opposition to the Islamist ideological paradigm being imposed on the
state came from the Bengali Muslims of East Pakistan[130] whose educated class,
according to a survey by social scientist Nasim Ahmad Jawed, preferred secularism
and focused on ethnic identity unlike educated West Pakistanis who tended to prefer
an Islamic identity.[131] The Islamist party [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamaat-e-Islami"] Jamaat-e-Islami considered Pakistan to be
an Islamic state and believed Bengali nationalism to be unacceptable. In the 1971
conflict over East Pakistan, the Jamaat-e-Islami fought the Bengali nationalists on the
Pakistan Army's side.[132] The conflict concluded with East Pakistan seceding and
the creation of independent Bangladesh.
After Pakistan's first ever general elections, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Pakistan"] 1973 Constitution was created by an
elected Parliament.[133] The Constitution declared Pakistan an Islamic Republic and
Islam as the state religion. It also stated that all laws would have to be brought into 
The Friday Prayers at the
 Badshahi Mosque in Lahore
accordance with the injunctions of Islam as laid down in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran"] Quran and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunnah"] Sunnah and that no law repugnant to such
injunctions could be enacted.[134] The 1973 Constitution also created certain institutions such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] Shariat Court and the
 Council of Islamic Ideology to channel the interpretation and application of Islam.[135]
Pakistan's leftist Prime Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto"] Zulfikar Ali Bhutto faced vigorous opposition which coalesced into a movement united
under the revivalist banner of Nizam-e-Mustafa ("Rule of the Prophet")[136] which aimed to establish an Islamic state
based on Sharia laws. Bhutto agreed to some Islamist demands before being overthrown in a coup.[137]
In 1977, after taking power from Bhutto in a coup d'état, General [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Zia-ul-Haq"] Zia-ul-Haq, who came from a religious
background,[138] committed himself to establishing an Islamic state and enforcing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia"] sharia law.[137] Zia established separate
Shariat judicial courts[139] and court benches[140] to judge legal cases using Islamic doctrine.[141] Zia bolstered the
influence of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulama"] ulama (Islamic clergy) and the Islamic parties.[141] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Zia-ul-Haq"] Zia-ul-Haq forged a strong alliance between the
 military and Deobandi institutions[142] and even though most Barelvi ulama[143] and only a few Deobandi scholars had
supported Pakistan's creation, Islamic state politics came to be mostly in favour of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deobandi"] Deobandi (and later Ahl-e-
Hadith/Salafi) institutions instead of Barelvi.[144] Sectarian tensions increased with Zia's anti-Shia policies.[145]
According to a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pew_Research_Center"] Pew Research Center (PEW) opinion poll, a majority of Pakistanis support making Sharia the official law
of the land.[146] In a survey of several Muslim countries, PEW also found that Pakistanis tend to identify with their
religion more than their nationality in contrast to Muslims in other nations such as Egypt, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia"] Indonesia and Jordan.[147]
Geography, environment, and climate
Page 9
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_Pakistan"] geography and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Pakistan"] climate of Pakistan are extremely diverse, and the country is
home to a wide variety of wildlife.[148] Pakistan covers an area of 881,913 km2
(340,509 sq mi), approximately equal to the combined land areas of France and the
United Kingdom. It is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_area"] 33rd-largest nation by total area, although this ranking
varies depending on how the disputed territory of Kashmir is counted. Pakistan has a
1,046 km (650 mi) coastline along the Arabian Sea and the Gulf of Oman in the
south[149] and land borders of 6,774 km (4,209 mi) in total: 2,430 km (1,510 mi) with
Afghanistan, 523 km (325 mi) with China, 2,912 km (1,809 mi) with India and
909 km (565 mi) with Iran.[150] It shares a marine border with Oman,[151] and is
separated from Tajikistan by the cold, narrow [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wakhan_Corridor"] Wakhan Corridor.[152] Pakistan
occupies a geopolitically important location at the crossroads of South Asia, the
Middle East, and Central Asia.[153]
Geologically, Pakistan is located in the Indus–Tsangpo Suture Zone and overlaps the
 Indian tectonic plate in its Sindh and Punjab provinces; Balochistan and most of
Khyber Pakhtunkhwa are within the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_plate"] Eurasian plate, mainly on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_plateau"] Iranian plateau.
 Gilgit-Baltistan and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azad_Kashmir"] Azad Kashmir lie along the edge of the Indian plate and hence
are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_Pakistan"] prone to violent earthquakes. This region has the highest rates of
 seismicity and the largest earthquakes in the Himalaya region.[154]
Ranging from the coastal areas of the south to the glaciated mountains
of the north, Pakistan's landscapes vary from plains to deserts, forests,
hills, and plateaus.[155] 
A satellite image showing the
topography of Pakistan
Pakistan is divided into three major geographic areas: the northern
highlands, the Indus River plain, and the Balochistan Plateau.[156] The
northern highlands contain the Karakoram, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_Kush"] Hindu Kush, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pamir_Mountains"] Pamir
mountain ranges (see [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountains_of_Pakistan"] mountains of Pakistan), which contain some of
 the world's highest peaks, including five of the fourteen eight-
thousanders (mountain peaks over 8,000 metres or 26,250 feet), which 
 Köppen climate classification of Pakistan
attract adventurers and mountaineers from all over the world, notably
 K2 (8,611 m or 28,251 ft) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanga_Parbat"] Nanga Parbat (8,126 m or 26,660 ft).[157] The Balochistan Plateau lies in the west and the
 Thar Desert in the east. The 1,609 km (1,000 mi) Indus River and its tributaries flow through the country from the
Kashmir region to the Arabian Sea. There is an expanse of alluvial plains along it in the Punjab and Sindh.[158]
The climate varies from tropical to temperate, with arid conditions in the coastal south. There is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsoon"] monsoon season with
frequent flooding due to heavy rainfall, and a dry season with significantly less rainfall or none at all. There are four
distinct seasons in Pakistan: a cool, dry winter from December through February; a hot, dry spring from March through
May; the summer rainy season, or southwest monsoon period, from June through September; and the retreating monsoon
period of October and November.[64] Rainfall varies greatly from year to year, and patterns of alternate flooding and
drought are common.[159]
Flora and fauna
The diversity of the landscape and climate in Pakistan allows a wide variety of trees and plants to flourish. The forests
range from coniferous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpine_plant"] alpine and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subalpine"] subalpine trees such as spruce, pine, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deodar_cedar"] deodar cedar in the extreme northern mountains
to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deciduous"] deciduous trees in most of the country (for example, the mulberry-like [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalbergia_sissoo"] shisham found in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulaiman_Mountains"] Sulaiman Mountains), to
palms such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coconut"] coconut and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera"] date in the southern Punjab, southern Balochistan, and all of Sindh. The western hills are home
to juniper, tamarisk, coarse grasses, and scrub plants. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mangrove"] Mangrove forests form much of the coastal wetlands along the coast
in the south.[160]
Coniferous forests are found at altitudes ranging from 1,000 to 4,000 metres (3,300 to 13,100 feet) in most of the northern
and northwestern highlands. In the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xeric"] xeric regions of Balochistan, date palm and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ephedra_(genus)"] Ephedra are common. In most of the
Punjab and Sindh, the Indus plains support tropical and subtropical dry and moist broadleaf forest as well as tropical and
xeric shrublands. These forests are mostly of mulberry, acacia, and eucalyptus.[161] About 2.2% or 1,687,000 hectares
(16,870 km2) of Pakistan was forested in 2010.[162]
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mulberry"]
Page 10
The fauna of Pakistan also reflects the country's varied climate. Around 668 bird species
are found there,[163] including crows, sparrows, mynas, hawks, falcons, and eagles.
 Palas, Kohistan, has a significant population of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_tragopan"] western tragopan.[164] Many birds
sighted in Pakistan are migratory, coming from Europe, Central Asia, and India.[165]
The southern plains are home to mongooses, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_Indian_civet"] small Indian civet, hares, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiatic_jackal"] Asiatic jackal,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_pangolin"] Indian pangolin, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jungle_cat"] jungle cat, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_cat"] desert cat. There are [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mugger_crocodile"] mugger crocodiles in the
Indus, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_boar"] wild boar, deer, porcupines, and small rodents in the surrounding areas. The Bear
sandy scrublands of central Pakistan are home to Asiatic jackals, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Striped_hyena"] striped hyenas, wildcats,
and leopards.[166][167] The lack of vegetative cover, the severe climate, and the impact of
grazing on the deserts have left wild animals in a precarious position. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinkara"] chinkara is the
only animal that can still be found in significant numbers in Cholistan. A small number of
 nilgai are found along the Pakistan–India border and in some parts of Cholistan.[166][168]
A wide variety of animals live in the mountainous north, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Polo_sheep"] Marco Polo sheep,
 the urial (a subspecies of wild sheep), the markhor goat, the ibex goat, the Asian black
bear, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Himalayan_brown_bear"] Himalayan brown bear.[166][169][170] Among the rare animals found in the
area are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snow_leopard"] snow leopard[169] and the blind [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_river_dolphin"] Indus river dolphin, of which there are 
Tibetan wolf
believed to be about 1,100 remaining, protected at the Indus River Dolphin Reserve in
Sindh.[169][171] In total, 174 mammals, 177 reptiles, 22 amphibians, 198 freshwater fish species and 5,000 species of
invertebrates (including insects) have been recorded in Pakistan.[163]
The flora and fauna of Pakistan suffer from a number of problems. Pakistan has the second-highest rate of deforestation in
 the world, which, along with hunting and pollution, has had adverse effects on the ecosystem. It had a 2019 Forest
Landscape Integrity Index mean score of 7.42/10, ranking it 41st globally out of 172 countries.[172] The government has
established a large number of protected areas, wildlife sanctuaries, and game reserves to address these issues.[163]
Government and politics
Pakistan's political experience is essentially related to the struggle of Indian
Muslims to regain the power they lost to British colonisation.[173] Pakistan is a
democratic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_republic"] parliamentary [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_parliamentary_republic"] federal republic, with Islam as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_religion"] state religion.[4] The
 first constitution was adopted in 1956 but suspended by Ayub Khan in 1958, who
replaced it with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Pakistan_of_1962"] second constitution in 1962.[67] A complete and
comprehensive [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Pakistan"] constitution was adopted in 1973, it was suspended by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Zia-ul-Haq"] Zia-ul-Haq
in 1977 but reinstated in 1985. This constitution is the country's most important
document, laying the foundations of the current government.[150] The Pakistani
military establishment has played an influential role in mainstream politics [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_Pakistan"] Parliament House
throughout [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_history_of_Pakistan"] Pakistan's political history.[67] The periods 1958–1971, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Pakistani_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1977–1988,
and 1999–2008 saw [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_coups_in_Pakistan"] military coups that resulted in the imposition of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martial_law_in_Pakistan"] martial law and military commanders who governed
as de facto presidents.[174] Today Pakistan has a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_system"] multi-party [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system"] parliamentary system with clear [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers"] division of powers and
 checks and balances among the branches of government. The first successful [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_Pakistani_general_election"] democratic transition occurred in May 2013.
Politics in Pakistan is centred on, and dominated by, a homegrown [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_philosophy"] social philosophy comprising a blend of ideas from
socialism, conservatism, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_way"] third way. As of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_Pakistani_general_election"] general elections held in 2013, the three main political parties in the
country are: the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centre-right_politics"] centre-right [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_in_Pakistan"] conservative [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Muslim_League_(N)"] Pakistan Muslim League-N; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centre-left_politics"] centre-left [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism_in_Pakistan"] socialist PPP; and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centre_politics"] centrist and
third-way [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Tehreek-e-Insaf"] Pakistan Movement for Justice (PTI).
 Head of State: The President, who is elected by an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electoral_College_of_Pakistan"] Electoral College is the ceremonial head of the state
 and is the civilian commander-in-chief of the Pakistan Armed Forces (with the Chairman Joint Chiefs of
Staff Committee as principal military adviser), but military appointments and key confirmations in the
armed forces are made by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan"] Prime Minister after reviewing the reports on candidates' merit and
performance. Almost all appointed officers in the judicature, military, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chairman_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff_Committee"] chairman joint chiefs, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff_Committee"] joint staff,
and legislature require the executive confirmation from the Prime Minister, whom the President must
consult by law. However, the powers to pardon and grant clemency lie with the President of Pakistan.
Legislative: The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameral"] bicameral legislature comprises a 104-member [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_of_Pakistan"] Senate ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_House"] upper house) and a 342-member
 National Assembly (lower house). Members of the National Assembly are elected through the first-past-
the-post system under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_adult_suffrage"] universal adult suffrage, representing electoral districts known as National
Assembly constituencies. According to the constitution, the 70 seats reserved for women and religious
Page 11
minorities are allocated to the political parties according to their proportional representation. Senate
members are elected by provincial legislators, with all the provinces having equal representation.
Executive: The Prime Minister is usually the leader of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majority_rule"] majority rule
party or a coalition in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_(Pakistan)"] National Assembly— the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_house"] lower house. The
Prime Minister serves as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government"] head of government and is designated to
exercise as the country's chief executive. The Prime Minister is
responsible for appointing a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Pakistan"] cabinet consisting of ministers and advisers
as well as running the government operations, taking and authorising
 executive decisions, appointments and recommendations of senior civil
servants that require executive confirmation of the Prime Minister.
 Provincial governments: Each of the four provinces has a similar system
 Prime Minister's Office  of government, with a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elections_in_Pakistan"] directly elected [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Provincial_Assemblies_of_Pakistan"] Provincial Assembly in which the
leader of the largest party or coalition is elected [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Minister_(Pakistan)"] Chief Minister. Chief
Ministers oversee the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_provincial_governments_of_Pakistan"] provincial governments and head the provincial
cabinet. It is common in Pakistan to have different ruling parties or coalitions in each of the provinces. The
provincial bureaucracy is headed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Secretary_(Pakistan)"] Chief Secretary, who is appointed by the Prime Minister. The
provincial assemblies have power to make laws and approve the provincial budget which is commonly
presented by the provincial finance minister every fiscal year. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Pakistan"] Provincial governors who are the
ceremonial heads of the provinces are appointed by the President.[150]
Judicature: The judiciary of Pakistan is a hierarchical system with two
classes of courts: the superior (or higher) judiciary and the
subordinate (or lower) judiciary. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Pakistan"] Chief Justice of Pakistan is the
 chief judge who oversees the judicature's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_system_of_Pakistan"] court system at all levels of
 command. The superior judiciary is composed of the Supreme Court
of Pakistan, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Shariat_Court"] Federal Shariat Court and five [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_courts_of_Pakistan"] high courts, with the
Supreme Court at the apex. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Pakistan"] Constitution of Pakistan entrusts the
superior judiciary with the obligation to preserve, protect and defend
the constitution. Other regions of Azad Kashmir and Gilgit-Baltistan
have separate court systems. 
 Supreme Court of Pakistan
Foreign relations 
Since Independence, Pakistan has attempted to balance its relations with foreign
nations.[175] Pakistan is a strong ally of China, with both countries placing
considerable importance on the maintenance of an extremely close and supportive
 special relationship.[176] It has also been a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally"] major non-NATO ally of the United States
ever since the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_against_terrorism"] war against terrorism – a status achieved in 2004.[177] Pakistan's
 foreign policy and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistani_geostrategy"] geostrategy mainly focus on the economy and security against
threats to its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalism_in_Pakistan"] national identity and territorial integrity, and on the cultivation of close
relations with other Muslim countries.[178]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir_conflict"] Kashmir conflict remains the major point of contention between Pakistan and
India; three of their [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_wars_and_conflicts"] four wars were fought over this territory.[179] Due partly to
difficulties in relations with its geopolitical rival India, Pakistan maintains close
political relations with Turkey and Iran,[180] and both countries have been a focal
point in Pakistan's foreign policy.[180] Saudi Arabia also maintains a respected
position in Pakistan's foreign policy.
President of Pakistan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayub_Khan_(general)"] Ayub Khan A non-signatory party of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons"] Treaty on Nuclear Non-Proliferation, Pakistan is an
 with US President John F.
Kennedy in 1961 
influential member of the IAEA.[181] In recent events, Pakistan has blocked an
 international treaty to limit [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fissile_material"] fissile material, arguing that the "treaty would target
Pakistan specifically".[182] In the 20th century, Pakistan's nuclear deterrence program
focused on countering India's nuclear ambitions in the region, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pokhran-II"] nuclear tests by
India eventually led Pakistan to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan%27s_nuclear_testing_series"] reciprocate to maintain a geopolitical balance as becoming a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Pakistan"] nuclear power.[183]
Currently, Pakistan maintains a policy of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N-deterrence"] credible minimum deterrence, calling its program vital [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_and_its_Nuclear_Deterrent_Program"] nuclear deterrence against
foreign aggression.[184][185]
Page 12
Located in the strategic and geopolitical corridor of the world's major maritime oil supply lines and communication fibre
optics, Pakistan has proximity to the natural resources of Central Asian countries.[186] Briefing on the country's foreign
policy in 2004, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Senate"] Pakistani senator reportedly explained: "Pakistan highlights sovereign equality of states, bilateralism,
mutuality of interests, and non-interference in each other's domestic affairs as the cardinal features of its foreign
policy."[187] Pakistan is an active member of the United Nations and has a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Representative_of_Pakistan_to_the_United_Nations"] Permanent Representative to represent
Pakistan's positions in international politics.[188] Pakistan has lobbied for the concept of "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enlightened_moderation"] enlightened moderation" in the
 Muslim world.[189] Pakistan is also a member of Commonwealth of Nations,[190] the South Asian Association for
 Regional Cooperation (SAARC),  the Economic Cooperation Organization (ECO),[191] and the G20 developing
nations.[192]
Due to ideological differences, Pakistan opposed the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union"] Soviet Union in the 1950s.
During the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War"] Soviet–Afghan War in the 1980s, Pakistan was one of the closest allies
of the United States.[187][193] Relations between Pakistan and Russia have greatly
improved since 1999, and co-operation in various sectors has increased.[194]
Pakistan has had an "on-and-off" relationship with the United States. A close ally
of the United States during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War"] Cold War, Pakistan's relationship with the US
soured in the 1990s when the latter [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pressler_amendment"] imposed sanctions because of Pakistan's
secretive nuclear development.[195] Since [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks"] 9/11, Pakistan has been a close ally of
the US on the issue of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterterrorism"] counterterrorism in the regions of the Middle East and
South Asia, with the US supporting Pakistan with aid money and
weapons.[196][197] Initially, the US-led war on terrorism led to an improvement in 
Pakistani Prime Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imran_Khan"] Imran Khan
 at the 2019 Shanghai Cooperation
Organisation summit
the relationship, but it was strained by a divergence of interests and resulting
mistrust during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)"] war in Afghanistan and by issues related to terrorism.[198] The Pakistani intelligence agency, the ISI,
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_and_state-sponsored_terrorism"] was accused of supporting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taliban"] Taliban insurgents in Afghanistan.[199][200][201]
Pakistan does not have [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan-Israel_relations"] diplomatic relations with Israel;[202] nonetheless, some Israeli citizens have visited the country on
tourist visas.[203] However, an exchange took place between the two countries using Turkey as a communication
conduit.[204] Despite Pakistan being the only country in the world that has not established [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia%E2%80%93Pakistan_relations"] diplomatic relations with
Armenia, an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenians_in_Pakistan"] Armenian community still resides in Pakistan.[205] Pakistan had warm relations with Bangladesh, despite
some initial strains in their relationship.
Relations with China
Pakistan was one of the first countries to establish formal diplomatic relations with the
 People's Republic of China, and the relationship continues to be strong since China's
 war with India in 1962, forming a special relationship.[207] From the 1960s to 1980s,
Pakistan greatly helped China in reaching out to the world's major countries and
helped facilitate US President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Nixon"] Richard Nixon's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_Nixon_visit_to_China"] state visit to China.[207] Despite the
change of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Pakistan"] governments in Pakistan and fluctuations in the regional and global
situation, China's policy in Pakistan continues to be a dominant factor at all
times.[207] In return, China is Pakistan's largest trading partner, and economic co-
operation has flourished, with substantial Chinese investment in Pakistan's
infrastructural expansion such as the Pakistani deep-water port at Gwadar. Friendly
Sino-Pakistani relations reached new heights as both countries signed 51 agreements
and Memorandums of Understanding (MoUs) in 2015 for co-operation in different
areas.[208] Both countries signed a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93Pakistan_Free_Trade_Agreement"] Free Trade Agreement in the 2000s, and Pakistan
continues to serve as China's communication bridge to the Muslim world.[209] In
2016, China announced that it will set up an anti-terrorism alliance with Pakistan,
Afghanistan, and Tajikistan.[210] In December 2018, Pakistan's government defended
China's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xinjiang_re-education_camps"] re-education camps for a million [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyghurs"] Uyghur Muslims.[211][212]
Emphasis on relations with Muslim world
After Independence, Pakistan vigorously pursued bilateral relations with other
Muslim countries[213] and made an active bid for leadership of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world"] Muslim world, or
at least for leadership in efforts to achieve unity.[214] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maulana_Muhammad_Ali_Jauhar"] Ali brothers had sought to 
 Pakistan Prime Minister Huseyn
Shaheed Suhrawardy with
Chinese Premier [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhou_Enlai"] Zhou Enlai
signing the Treaty of Friendship
Between China and Pakistan.
Pakistan is host to China's
largest embassy.[206]
Page 13
project Pakistan as the natural leader of the Islamic world, in part due to its large manpower and military strength.[215] A
top-ranking [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All_India_Muslim_League"] Muslim League leader, Khaliquzzaman, declared that Pakistan would bring together all Muslim countries into
Islamistan – a pan-Islamic entity.[216]
 Such developments (along with Pakistan's creation) did not get American approval, and British Prime Minister Clement
Attlee voiced international opinion at the time by stating that he wished that India and Pakistan would re-unite.[217] Since
most of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world"] Arab world was undergoing a nationalist awakening at the time, there was little attraction to Pakistan's Pan-
Islamic aspirations.[218] Some of the Arab countries saw the 'Islamistan' project as a Pakistani attempt to dominate other
Muslim states.[219]
Pakistan vigorously championed the right of self-determination for Muslims around the world. Pakistan's efforts for the
independence movements of Indonesia, Algeria, Tunisia, Morocco, and Eritrea were significant and initially led to close
ties between these countries and Pakistan.[220] However, Pakistan also masterminded an attack on the Afghan city of
 Jalalabad during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghan_Civil_War_(1989%E2%80%9392)"] Afghan Civil War to establish an Islamic government there. Pakistan had wished to foment an 'Islamic
Revolution' that would transcend national borders, covering Pakistan, Afghanistan, and Central Asia.[221]
 On the other hand, Pakistan's relations with Iran have been strained at times due to sectarian tensions.[222] Iran and Saudi
Arabia used Pakistan as a battleground for their proxy sectarian war, and by the 1990s Pakistan's support for the Sunni
Taliban organisation in Afghanistan became a problem for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia"] Shia Iran, which opposed a Taliban-controlled
Afghanistan.[223] Tensions between Iran and Pakistan intensified in 1998 when Iran accused Pakistan of war crimes after
Pakistani warplanes had bombarded Afghanistan's last Shia stronghold in support of the Taliban.[224]
Pakistan is an influential and founding member of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation"] Organisation of Islamic Cooperation (OIC). Maintaining cultural,
political, social, and economic relations with the Arab world and other countries in the Muslim world is a vital factor in
Pakistan's foreign policy.[225]
