was found to be 4,444,437.[490]
Hindus are found in all provinces of
Pakistan but are mostly concentrated
in Sindh, where they account for
 8.73% of the population.[5] Umerkot 
Havana at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shri_Hinglaj_Mata_temple"] Shri Hinglaj Mata temple
shakti peetha, the largest Hindu
pilgrimage centre in Pakistan. The
annual Hinglaj Yathra is attended by
more than 250,000 people.[487]
district (52.15%) is the only Hindu majority district in Pakistan. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tharparkar_District"] Tharparkar district
has the highest population of Hindus in terms of absolute terms. The four districts in Sindh- Umerkot, Tharparkar,
 Mirpurkhas and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanghar_District"] Sanghar hosts more than half of the Hindu population in Pakistan.[481]
At the time of Pakistan's creation, the 'hostage theory' gained currency. According to this theory, the Hindu minority in
Pakistan was to be given a fair deal in Pakistan in order to ensure the protection of the Muslim minority in India.[491]
However, Khawaja Nazimuddin, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Pakistan"] second [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan"] Prime Minister of Pakistan, stated:
Page 29
I do not agree that religion is a private affair of the individual nor do I agree that in an Islamic state every
citizen has identical rights, no matter what his caste, creed or faith be.[492]
Some Hindus in Pakistan feel that they are treated as second-class citizens and many have continued to migrate to
 India.[467] Pakistani Hindus faced riots after the Babri Masjid demolition[493] and have experienced other attacks, forced
conversions, and abductions.[494]
Christianity and other religions
Christians formed the next largest religious minority after Hindus, with 1.27% of
the population following it.[436] The highest concentration of Christians in
 Pakistan is in Lahore District (5%) in Punjab province and in Islamabad Capital
Territory (over 4% Christian). There is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Pakistan"] Roman Catholic community in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karachi"] Karachi
that was established by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goa"] Goan and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_people"] Tamil migrants when Karachi's infrastructure
was being developed by the British during the colonial administration between
World War I and World War II.[481]
They are followed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Pakistan"] Bahá'í Faith, which had a following of 30,000, then
Sikhism, Buddhism, and Zoroastrianism, each back then claiming 20,000
adherents,[495] and a very small [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainism_in_Pakistan"] community of Jains.
1.0% of the population identified as atheist in 2005. However, the figure rose
to 2.0% in 2012 according to Gallup.[496] 
 Sacred Heart Cathedral, Lahore
Culture and society
 Civil society in Pakistan is largely hierarchical, emphasising local cultural
etiquette and traditional Islamic values that govern personal and political life.
The basic family unit is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extended_family"] extended family,[497] although for socio-
 economic reasons there has been a growing trend towards nuclear
 families.[498] The traditional dress for both men and women is the Shalwar
Kameez; trousers, jeans, and shirts are also popular among men.[44] In recent
decades, the middle class has increased to around 35 million and the upper 
Christian Proportion of each Pakistani
District in 2017 according to the Pakistan
Bureau of Statistics
and upper-middle classes to around 17 million, and power is shifting from
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr"] rural landowners to the urbanised elites.[499] Pakistani festivals, including Eid-ul-
Fitr, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_al-Adha"] Eid-ul-Azha, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramadan"] Ramazan,  Christmas, Easter, Holi, and Diwali, are mostly
religious in origin.[497] Increasing globalisation has resulted in Pakistan ranking
56th on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.T._Kearney"] A.T. Kearney/FP [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Globalization_Index"] Globalization Index.[500]
Clothing, arts, and fashion
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shalwar_kameez"] Shalwar Kameez is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_dress"] national dress of Pakistan and is worn by both men
 and women in all four provinces: Punjab, Sindh, Balochistan, and Khyber- [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truck_art_in_Pakistan"] Truck art is a distinctive feature of
Pakhtunkhwa, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azad_Kashmir"] Azad Kashmir. Each province has its own style of Shalwar Pakistani culture.
Kameez. Pakistanis wear clothes in a range of exquisite colours and designs and in
type of fabric (silk, chiffon, cotton, etc.). Besides the national dress, domestically
tailored [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suit_(clothing)"] suits and neckties are often worn by men, and are customary in offices, schools, and social gatherings.[501]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistani_fashion"] fashion industry has flourished in the changing environment of the fashion world. Since Pakistan came into being, its
fashion has evolved in different phases and developed a unique identity. Today, Pakistani fashion is a combination of
traditional and modern dress and has become a mark of Pakistani culture. Despite modern trends, regional and traditional
forms of dress have developed their own significance as a symbol of native tradition. This regional fashion continues to
 evolve into both more modern and purer forms. The Pakistan Fashion Design Council based in Lahore organizes PFDC
Fashion Week and the Fashion Pakistan Council based in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karachi"] Karachi organizes [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_Pakistan_Week"] Fashion Pakistan Week. Pakistan's first
fashion week was held in November 2009.[502]
Page 30
Media and entertainment
The private [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newspapers_in_Pakistan"] print media, state-owned [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Television_Corporation"] Pakistan Television Corporation (PTV), and
 Pakistan Broadcasting Corporation (PBC) for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Pakistan"] radio were the dominant media
outlets until the beginning of the 21st century. Pakistan now has a large network of
domestic, privately owned 24-hour [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/News_channels_in_Pakistan"] news media and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_in_Pakistan"] television channels.[503] A
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index"] 2016 report by the Reporters Without Borders ranked Pakistan 147th on the Press
Freedom Index, while at the same time terming the Pakistani media "among the
freest in Asia when it comes to covering the squabbling among politicians."[504]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC"] BBC terms the Pakistani media "among the most outspoken in South
Asia".[505] Pakistani media has also played a vital role in exposing
corruption.[506] 
People in traditional clothing in
 Neelum District
The Lollywood, Kariwood, Punjabi and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashto_cinema"] Pashto film industry is based in Karachi, Lahore and Peshawar. While
 Bollywood films were banned from public cinemas from 1965 until 2008, they have remained an important part of
popular culture.[507] In contrast to the ailing Pakistani film industry, Urdu [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistani_dramas"] televised dramas and theatrical performances
 continue to be popular, as many entertainment media outlets air them regularly.[508] Urdu dramas dominate the television
entertainment industry, which has launched critically acclaimed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miniseries"] miniseries and featured popular actors and actresses since
the 1990s.[509] In the 1960s–1970s, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistani_pop_music"] pop music and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disco_Deewane"] disco (1970s) dominated the country's music industry. In the 1980s–
 1990s, British influenced rock music appeared and jolted the country's entertainment industry.[510] In the 2000s, heavy
metal music gained popular and critical acclaim.[511]
Pakistani music ranges from diverse forms of provincial folk music and traditional styles such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qawwali"] Qawwali and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazal"] Ghazal
Gayaki to modern musical forms that fuse traditional and western music.[512][513] Pakistan has many famous folk singers.
The arrival of Afghan refugees in the western provinces has stimulated interest in Pashto music, although there has been
intolerance of it in some places.[514]
Diaspora
According to the UN Department of Economic and Social Affairs, Pakistan has the sixth-largest diaspora in the
world.[455] Statistics gathered by the Pakistani government show that there are around 7 million [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pakistan_people&action=edit&redlink=1"] Pakistanis residing
abroad, with the vast majority living in the Middle East, Europe, and North America.[515] Pakistan ranks 10th in the world
for remittances sent home.[307][516] The largest inflow of remittances, as of 2016, is from Saudi Arabia, amounting to
 $5.9 billion.[517] The term Overseas Pakistani is officially recognised by the Government of Pakistan. The Ministry of
Overseas Pakistanis was established in 2008 to deal exclusively with all matters of overseas Pakistanis such as attending to
their needs and problems, developing projects for their welfare, and working for resolution of their problems and issues.
Overseas Pakistanis are the second-largest source of foreign exchange remittances to Pakistan after exports. Over the last
several years, home remittances have maintained a steadily rising trend, with a more than 100% increase from
US$8.9 billion in 2009–10 to US$19.9 billion in 2015–16.[306][516]
The Overseas Pakistani Division (OPD) was created in September 2004 within the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Labour_(Pakistan)"] Ministry of Labour (MoL). It has since
recognised the importance of overseas Pakistanis and their contribution to the nation's economy. Together with
Community Welfare Attaches (CWAs) and the Overseas Pakistanis Foundation (OPF), the OPD is making efforts to
improve the welfare of Pakistanis who reside abroad. The division aims to provide better services through improved
facilities at airports, and suitable schemes for housing, education, and health care. It also facilitates the reintegration into
 society of returning overseas Pakistanis. Notable members of the Pakistani diaspora include the London Mayor Sadiq
 Khan, the UK cabinet member Sajid Javid, the former UK Conservative Party chair Baroness Warsi, the singers Zayn
Malik and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nadia_Ali_(singer)"] Nadia Ali, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT"] MIT physics Professor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nergis_Mavalvala"] Dr. Nergis Mavalvala, the actors [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riz_Ahmed"] Riz Ahmed and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kumail_Nanjiani"] Kumail Nanjiani, the
 businessmen Shahid Khan and Sir Anwar Pervez, Boston University professors Adil Najam and Hamid Nawab, Texas
A&M professor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Suhail_Zubairy"] Muhammad Suhail Zubairy, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yale"] Yale professor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sara_Suleri"] Sara Suleri, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UC_San_Diego"] UC San Diego professor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farooq_Azam"] Farooq Azam and the
historian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayesha_Jalal"] Ayesha Jalal.
Literature and philosophy
Pakistan has literature in Urdu, Sindhi, Punjabi, Pashto, Baluchi, Persian, English, and many other languages.[518] The
 Pakistan Academy of Letters is a large literary community that promotes literature and poetry in Pakistan and abroad.[519]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Library_of_Pakistan"] National Library publishes and promotes literature in the country. Before the 19th century, Pakistani literature
Page 31
consisted mainly of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyric_poetry"] lyric and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sufi_poetry"] religious poetry and mystical and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistani_folklore"] folkloric works. During the
colonial period, native literary figures were influenced by western [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_realism"] literary realism and took up
increasingly varied topics and narrative forms. Prose fiction is now very popular.[520][521]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_poets"] national poet of Pakistan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Iqbal"] Muhammad Iqbal, wrote
poetry in Urdu and Persian. He was a strong proponent
of the political and spiritual revival of Islamic
civilisation and encouraged Muslims all over the world
to bring about a successful revolution.[523] Well-known
figures in contemporary Pakistani Urdu literature
 Muhammad Iqbal,
Pakistan's national
poet who conceived
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conception_of_Pakistan"] idea of Pakistan 
 include Josh Malihabadi Faiz Ahmed Faiz and Saadat
Hasan Manto. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadequain"] Sadequain and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulgee"] Gulgee are known for
their calligraphy and paintings.[521] The Sufi poets
 Shah Abdul Latif, Bulleh Shah, Mian Muhammad
Bakhsh, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khawaja_Farid"] Khawaja Farid enjoy considerable
popularity in Pakistan.[524] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirza_Kalich_Beg"] Mirza Kalich Beg has been
termed the father of modern Sindhi prose.[525] Historically, philosophical
development in the country was dominated by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Iqbal"] Muhammad Iqbal, Sir Syed Ahmad
Khan, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Asad"] Muhammad Asad, Maududi, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammad_Ali_Jouhar"] Mohammad Ali Johar.[526] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomb_of_Shah_Rukn-e-Alam"] Tomb of Shah Rukn-e-Alam is
part of Pakistan's Sufi heritage.[522]
 Ideas from British and American philosophy greatly shaped philosophical development in Pakistan. Analysts such as M.
M. Sharif and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syed_Zafarul_Hasan"] Zafar Hassan established the first major Pakistani philosophical movement in 1947.[527] After the 1971 war,
philosophers such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jalaludin_Abdur_Rahim"] Jalaludin Abdur Rahim, Gianchandani, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malik_Meraj_Khalid"] Malik Khalid incorporated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism"] Marxism into Pakistan's
philosophical thinking. Influential work by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manzoor_Ahmad"] Manzoor Ahmad, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jon_Elia"] Jon Elia, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasan_Askari_Rizvi"] Hasan Askari Rizvi, and Abdul Khaliq brought
mainstream social, political, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytical_philosophy"] analytical philosophy to the fore in academia.[528] Works by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noam_Chomsky"] Noam Chomsky have
influenced philosophical ideas in various fields of social and political philosophy.[529]
Architecture
Four periods are recognised in Pakistani architecture: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Pakistan#Early_history"] pre-Islamic, Islamic,
colonial, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Pakistan#Independence"] post-colonial. With the beginning of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_civilization"] Indus civilization around the
middle of the 3rd millennium BCE,[530] an advanced urban culture developed for
the first time in the region, with large buildings, some of which survive to this
day.[531] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-daro"] Mohenjo Daro, Harappa, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kot_Diji"] Kot Diji are among the pre-Islamic
settlements that are now tourist attractions.[157] The rise of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism"] Buddhism and the
influence of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_campaign_of_Alexander_the_Great"] Greek civilisation led to the development of a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Buddhism"] Greco-Buddhist
style,[532] starting from the 1st century CE. The high point of this era was the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gandara_art"] Gandhara style. An example of Buddhist architecture is the ruins of the Buddhist
monastery [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Takht_Bhai"] Takht-i-Bahi in Khyber-Pakhtunkhwa.[533] 
 Minar-e-Pakistan is a national
monument marking Pakistan's
independence movement.
The arrival of Islam in what is today Pakistan meant the sudden end of Buddhist
architecture in the area and a smooth transition to the predominantly pictureless [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_architecture"] Islamic architecture. The most important
 Indo-Islamic-style building still standing is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rukn-e-Alam"] tomb of the Shah Rukn-i-Alam in Multan. During the Mughal era, design
elements of Persian-Islamic architecture were fused with and often produced playful forms of Hindustani art. Lahore, as
the occasional residence of Mughal rulers, contains many important buildings from the empire. Most prominent among
 them are the Badshahi Mosque, the fortress of Lahore with the famous Alamgiri Gate, the colourful, Mughal-style Wazir
Khan Mosque,[534] the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shalimar_Gardens_(Lahore)"] Shalimar Gardens in Lahore, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahjahan_Mosque"] Shahjahan Mosque in Thatta. In the British colonial period,
predominantly functional buildings of the Indo-European representative style developed from a mixture of European and
Indian-Islamic components. Post-colonial national identity is expressed in modern structures such as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_Mosque"] Faisal Mosque,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minar-e-Pakistan"] Minar-e-Pakistan, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazar-e-Quaid"] Mazar-e-Quaid. Several examples of architectural infrastructure demonstrating the influence
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture_of_the_United_Kingdom"] British design can be found in Lahore, Peshawar, and Karachi.[535]
Food and drink
Traditional food
Page 32
Pakistani cuisine is similar to that of other regions of South Asia, with some of it
being originated from the royal kitchens of 16th-century Mughal emperors.[537]
 Most of those dishes have their roots in British, Indian, Central Asian and Middle
Eastern cuisine.[538] Unlike Middle Eastern cuisine, Pakistani cooking uses large
quantities of spices, herbs, and seasoning. Garlic, ginger, turmeric, red chili, and
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garam_masala"] garam masala are used in most dishes, and home cooking regularly includes curry,
 roti, a thin flatbread made from wheat, is a staple food, usually served with curry,
meat, vegetables, and lentils. Rice is also common; it is served plain, fried with
spices, and in sweet dishes.[153][539]
 Lassi is a traditional drink in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjab_region"] Punjab region. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistani_tea_culture"] Black tea with milk and sugar is
popular throughout Pakistan and is consumed daily by most of the
population.[44][540] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sohan_halwa"] Sohan halwa is a popular sweet dish from the southern region
of Punjab province and is enjoyed all over Pakistan.[541] 
Located on the bank of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Sea"] Arabian Sea
in Karachi, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_Grand"] Port Grand is one of the
largest food streets of Asia.[536]
Sports
Most sports played in Pakistan originated and were substantially developed by athletes and sports fans from the United
Kingdom who introduced them during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Raj"] British Raj. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_hockey"] Field hockey is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_sport"] national sport of Pakistan; it has won three gold
medals in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympic_Games"] Olympic Games held in 1960, 1968, and 1984.[542] Pakistan has also won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hockey_World_Cup"] Hockey World Cup a record
four times, held in 1971, 1978, 1982, and 1994.[543]
Cricket, however, is the most popular game across the country.[544] The country
has had an array of success in the sport over the years, and has the distinct
achievement of having won each of the major [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Cricket_Council"] ICC international cricket
 tournaments: ICC Cricket World Cup, ICC World Twenty20, and ICC Champions
Trophy; as well as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICC_Test_Championship"] ICC Test Championship.[545] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_national_cricket_team"] cricket team (known as
 Shaheen) won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup"] Cricket World Cup held in 1992; it was runner-up once, in
1999. Pakistan was runner-up in the inaugural [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007_ICC_World_Twenty20"] World Twenty20 (2007) in South
Africa and won the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Twenty20"] World Twenty20 in England in 2009. In March 2009,
militants [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_attack_on_the_Sri_Lanka_national_cricket_team"] attacked the touring [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lankan_cricket_team"] Sri Lankan cricket team,[546] after which no
international cricket was played in Pakistan until May 2015, when the
 Zimbabwean team agreed to a tour. Pakistan also won the 2017 ICC Champions
Trophy by defeating arch-rivals [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India_national_cricket_team"] India in the final.
 Pakistan Super League is one of the largest cricket leagues of the world with a
brand value of about ₨32.26 billion (US$200 million).[547] 
 Gaddafi Stadium, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahore"] Lahore is the 3rd
largest cricket stadium in Pakistan
with a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seating_capacity"] seating capacity of 27,000
spectators.
 Association Football is the second most played sports in Pakistan and it is organised and regulated by the Pakistan
Football Federation.[548] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football_in_Pakistan"] Football in Pakistan is as old as the country itself. Shortly after the creation of Pakistan in 1947,
the Pakistan Football Federation (PFF) was created, and Muhammad Ali Jinnah became its first Patron-in-Chief.[549] The
highest football division in Pakistan is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan_Premier_League"] Pakistan Premier League.[550] Pakistan is known as one of the best
manufacturer of the official [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup"] FIFA World Cup ball.[551] The best football players to play for Pakistan are Kaleemullah,
 Zesh Rehman, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Essa"] Muhammad Essa, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haroon_Yousaf"] Haroon Yousaf and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Adil"] Muhammad Adil.
Pakistan has hosted or co-hosted several international sporting events: the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_South_Asian_Games"] 1989 and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_South_Asian_Games"] 2004 South Asian Games; the 1984,
 1993, 1996 and 2003 World Squash Championships; the 1987 and 1996 Cricket World Cup; and the 1990 Hockey World
Cup.
Pakistan is set to host the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_South_Asian_Games"] 2023 South Asian Games.

14. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robin_Coningham"] Coningham, Robin; Young, Ruth (2015), The Archaeology of South Asia: From the Indus to Asoka, c.
6500 BCE – 200 CE, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambridge_University_Press"] Cambridge University Press Quote: ""Mehrgarh remains one of the key sites in
South Asia because it has provided the earliest known undisputed evidence for farming and pastoral
communities in the region, and its plant and animal material provide clear evidence for the ongoing
manipulation, and domestication, of certain species. Perhaps most importantly in a South Asian context,
the role played by zebu makes this a distinctive, localised development, with a character completely
different to other parts of the world. Finally, the longevity of the site, and its articulation with the
neighbouring site of Nausharo (c. 2800—2000 BCE), provides a very clear continuity from South Asia's
first farming villages to the emergence of its first cities (Jarrige, 1984)."

81. [URL: "https://www.jstor.org/stable/23726109"] Kumarasingham, Harshan (2013), THE 'TROPICAL DOMINIONS': THE APPEAL OF DOMINION
STATUS IN THE DECOLONISATION OF INDIA, PAKISTAN AND CEYLON, vol. 23 (https://www.jstor.or
 g/stable/23726109), Transactions of the Royal Historical Society, p. 223, JSTOR 23726109 (https://www.j
stor.org/stable/23726109), "Few today, including those who work on the subcontinent, recollect that India,
Pakistan and Sri Lanka did not become republics the day British rule ended. Even distinguished scholars
of Empire like Perry Anderson and A. G. Hopkins have made the common assumption that India naturally
became a republic upon independence on 15 August 1947. Instead, all three of these South Asian states
began their independent life as Realms within the British Commonwealth and mirrored the style and
institutions of the Dominions of Canada, Australia, South Africa and New Zealand. Though their
sovereignty was in no way impaired by this seemingly ambiguous position they all held the British
sovereign as their head of state who was represented in each capital by a governor- general appointed on
the advice of the local prime minister. India, Pakistan and Ceylon were Realms from 1947 to 1950, 1947
to 1956 and 1948 to 1972 respectively."

87. Hussain, Rizwan. [URL: "http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616"] "Pakistan" (http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616). The Oxford
Encyclopedia of the Islamic World. "Mawlānā Shabbīr Ahmad Usmānī, a respected Deobandī ʿālim
(scholar) who was appointed to the prestigious position of Shaykh al-Islām of Pakistan in 1949, was the
first to demand that Pakistan become an Islamic state. But Mawdūdī and his Jamāʿat-i Islāmī played the
central part in the demand for an Islamic constitution. Mawdūdī demanded that the Constituent Assembly
make an unequivocal declaration affirming the "supreme sovereignty of God" and the supremacy of the
sharīʿah as the basic law of Pakistan."
88. Hussain, Rizwan. [URL: "http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616"] "Pakistan" (http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616). The Oxford
Encyclopedia of the Islamic World. "The first important result of the combined efforts of the Jamāʿat-i
Islāmī and the ʿulamāʿ was the passage of the Objectives Resolution in March 1949, whose formulation
reflected compromise between traditionalists and modernists. The resolution embodied "the main
principles on which the constitution of Pakistan is to be based". It declared that "sovereignty over the
entire universe belongs to God Almighty alone and the authority which He has delegated to the State of
Pakistan through its people for being exercised within the limits prescribed by Him is a sacred trust", that
"the principles of democracy, freedom, equality, tolerance and social justice, as enunciated by Islam shall
be fully observed", and that "the Muslims shall be enabled to order their lives in the individual and
collective spheres in accord with the teaching and requirements of Islam as set out in the Holy Qurʿan and
Sunna". The Objectives Resolution has been reproduced as a preamble to the constitutions of 1956,
1962, and 1973."

131. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=X2_FAgAAQBAJ&pg=PT37"] Cochrane, Iain (2009). The Causes of the Bangladesh War (https://books.google.com/books?id=X2_FAg
AAQBAJ&pg=PT37). ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4452-4043-5"] 1-4452-4043-5. "The social scientist, Nasim Ahmad Jawed has
conducted a survey of nationalism in pre-divided Pakistan and identifies the links between religion,
politics and nationalism in both wings of Pakistan. His findings are fascinating and go some way to
explain the differing attitudes of West and East Pakistan to the relationship between Islam and Pakistani
nationalism and how this affected the views of people in both wings, especially the views of the peoples
of both wings towards each other. In 1969, Jawed conducted a survey on the type of national identity that
was used by educated professional people. He found that just over 60% in the East wing professed to
have a secular national identity. However, in the West wing, the same figure professed an Islamic and not
a secular identity. Furthermore, the same figure in the East wing described their identity in terms of their
ethnicity and not in terms of Islam. He found that the opposite was the case in the West wing where Islam
was stated to be more important than ethnicity."

actors on Jalalabad, the first major urban centre across the Khyber Pass from Pakistan, with the aim

can't get an education after matriculation because colleges ask for the identity cards but the National
Database Registration Authority has never accepted us as Pakistani citizens.' Shaikh said that over three
million Bengalis and Biharis were grateful to the government for accepting them as Pakistani citizens. 'We
postponed a hunger strike planned for March 25 after the government made decisions', he added. 'We
can go on a hunger strike, if our rights are not given.' He claimed that there were 200 settlements of
Bengali-speaking people across the country, including 132 in Karachi. They populate different parts of
Pakistan, including Thatta, Badin, Hyderabad, Tando Adam and Lahore."

476. The 1998 Pakistani census states that there are 291,000 (0.22%) Ahmadis in Pakistan. However, the
Ahmadiyya Muslim Community has boycotted the census since 1974 which renders official Pakistani
figures to be inaccurate. Independent groups have estimated the Pakistani Ahmadiyya population to be
somewhere between 2 million and 5 million Ahmadis. However, the 4 million figure is the most quoted
figure and is approximately 2.2% of the country. See:

484. Hussain, Rizwan. [URL: "http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616"] "Pakistan" (http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616). The Oxford
Encyclopedia of the Islamic World. "Sūfī Islam in Pakistan is represented at two levels. The first is the
populist Sufism of the rural masses, associated with unorthodox religious rituals and practices, belief in
the intercessory powers of saints, pilgrimage and veneration at their shrines, and a binding spiritual
relationship between the shaykh or pir (master) and murīd (disciple). Many Muslims in rural areas of
Pakistan, where orthodox Islam has yet to penetrate effectively, identify themselves with some pir, living or
dead, and seek his intercession for the solution of their worldly problems and for salvation in the
hereafter."
485. Hussain, Rizwan. [URL: "http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616"] "Pakistan" (http://www.oxfordislamicstudies.com/article/opr/t236/e0616). The Oxford
Encyclopedia of the Islamic World. "The other strain is that of scholastic or intellectual Sufism, a recent
phenomenon based in urban areas and becoming increasingly popular in educated circles. Influenced by
the writings of the medieval theologian al-Ghazālī (d. 1111), the Sūfī reformer Shaykh Aḥmad Sirhindī
(d. 1624), and Shāh Walī Allāh (d. 1762), and by the spiritual experiences of the masters of the
Suhrawardī and Naqshbandī orders, these modern Sūfīs are rearticulating Islamic metaphysics as an
answer to Western materialism."
